## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: materials science / solid mechanics (thermo-mechanical constitutive modeling)
**Analysis**: The variables are stress (sigma), strain (epsilon), and temperature (T), which is the standard setting for thermoelasticity and temperature-dependent plasticity/flow-stress constitutive laws. Common relationships include elastic stress–strain laws with temperature-dependent modulus, thermal strain offsets, and strain-hardening with thermal softening.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke’s law (1D linear elasticity): sigma = c0 * epsilon (small strain, isothermal elastic response)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (linear in T): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (elastic stiffness varies approximately linearly with temperature)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (exponential in T): sigma = c0 * exp(c1 * T) * epsilon (stiffness changes rapidly with temperature, empirical fit)
- Thermoelastic stress with thermal strain offset: sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * (T - c2)) (mechanical strain = total strain minus thermal expansion strain)
- Quadratic elastic nonlinearity (Murnaghan/Landau-type 1D truncation): sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (moderate strains, nonlinear elasticity)
- Temperature-dependent nonlinear elasticity: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon + (c2 + c3 * T) * epsilon**2 (nonlinear elastic coefficients change with temperature)
- Hollomon strain hardening with thermal softening factor: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (plastic flow stress vs strain with temperature sensitivity)
- Power-law hardening with linear thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (c2 + c3 * T) (empirical thermal softening over limited T-range)
- Exponential hardening (Voce-like in 1D form): sigma = c0 + c1 * (c2 - exp(c3 * epsilon)) (stress approaches a saturation level with increasing strain)
- Ramberg–Osgood rearranged (implicit usually; explicit surrogate): sigma = c0 * ( (c1 * epsilon)**c2 ) (captures gradual transition from elastic to plastic in a single monotone curve)
- Johnson–Cook-like (strain hardening × thermal softening; no strain-rate term): sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 + c4 * (T - c5)**c6) (metal plasticity with thermal softening referenced to a temperature)
- Neo-Hookean-like 1D true-stress form using stretch (lambda = 1 + epsilon): sigma = c0 * ((1 + epsilon) - c1 / (1 + epsilon)**2) (finite-strain hyperelastic-inspired structure)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Elastic regime often appears as proportionality in epsilon; deviations suggest adding epsilon**2, epsilon**3 terms (nonlinear elasticity at higher strain).
- Thermal expansion shifts the zero-stress strain: a best fit may require sigma depending on (epsilon - c*(T - c)) rather than epsilon alone.
- Thermal softening typically reduces stress with increasing T; look for multiplicative factors like (c0 + c1 * T) or exp(c * T) applied to an otherwise isothermal stress–strain law.
- Plastic strain hardening commonly produces concave-down sigma(epsilon) on log-log plots, consistent with power-law epsilon**c; saturation at large strain suggests Voce/exponential-to-limit forms.
- Finite-strain effects can introduce singular/strong curvature near epsilon = -1 when using stretch-based terms like 1/(1+epsilon)**n; such structure may appear if data includes large compressive strains.
- If sigma varies with T mostly through stiffness (slope) rather than offset, prioritize E(T)*epsilon forms; if it varies through an offset, prioritize (epsilon - alpha*(T-T0)).
- Coupled temperature–strain nonlinearity (e.g., coefficients of epsilon**2 depending on T) indicates mechanisms like temperature-dependent hardening modulus; model via (c0 + c1*T)*epsilon + (c2 + c3*T)*epsilon**2.
- If curves at different T collapse when sigma is normalized by a T-dependent factor, a separable multiplicative form sigma = f(epsilon)*g(T) is often effective.
- If there is an apparent yield-like knee but no explicit yield variable, approximate with smooth transitions using sums of low- and high-strain terms (e.g., linear + power-law) rather than sharp piecewise fits.

GT (fixed):  
\[
61.5603538772\,\epsilon^{0.4776400562}\exp\!\left(-\frac{55.8810511986}{8.314\,T}\right)\;+\;7.64107225026\,\epsilon^{3}(T-344.45959227)
\]
So GT is exactly the sum of:
1) an Arrhenius-type term \(A\,\epsilon^{p}\exp(-K/T)\) with **negative** \(1/T\) exponent and **non-integer** \(\epsilon\)-power \(p\approx 0.47764\); and  
2) a polynomial term \(7.6410\,\epsilon^3 T - 7.6410\cdot 344.4596\,\epsilon^3\), i.e. **two** \(\epsilon^3\) terms: one proportional to \(T\) and one constant in \(T\).

A candidate can match only if it can represent:
- an \(\epsilon^{0.47764}\exp(c/T)\) term with \(c=-55.8810511986/8.314\) (so \(c<0\)), and
- both \((\text{const})\cdot T\epsilon^3\) and \((\text{const})\cdot \epsilon^3\) (the \(-344.4596\) shift).

Also, “conditional equivalence” lets \(\mathrm{Abs}(\epsilon)=\epsilon\) assuming \(\epsilon\ge 0\), but it does **not** let \(\epsilon^4\) become \(\epsilon^3\), etc.

Now check candidates:

1. Has \(T c0 \epsilon^3\) and an exp term \(c7 e^{c8/T}|\epsilon|^{c9}\) (good), but the remaining rational terms \(c3\epsilon/(c4\epsilon+c5)+c6/(c4\epsilon+c5)\) cannot be made identically equal to the needed \(-(\text{const})\epsilon^3\) for all \(\epsilon\) unless they are zero; setting them zero leaves no standalone \(\epsilon^3\) constant term. **No**.

2. Has \(T\cdot(\text{const})\epsilon^3\) and an exp-power term. But all non-exp \(\epsilon^3\) terms are either multiplied by \(T\) or are \(\epsilon^3\) with free constants? Actually it has only \(T c0|\epsilon|^3\) plus several \(|\epsilon|^3\) terms (c2,c3) yes: \(c2|\epsilon|^3+c3|\epsilon|^3\) can form the constant \(\epsilon^3\) term. However it also has a \(|\epsilon|^4\) term \(c1|\epsilon|^4\) which must be set to 0. Then we can set exp exponent sign and \(\epsilon\)-power to 0.47764. This one *could* match structurally. But note: the exp is \(e^{c5/T}\) (fine; choose \(c5=-55.8810511986/8.314\)). So candidate 2 can represent:
- \(T c0 \epsilon^3\) (set \(c0=7.641072250261916\))
- constant \(\epsilon^3\) term via \(c2+c3\) (set \(c2+c3=-7.641072250261916\cdot 344.4595922700062\))
- exp term via \(c4 e^{c5/T}\epsilon^{c6}\) (set \(c4=61.560353877200875\), \(c5=-55.88105119862867/8.314\), \(c6=0.47764005618501093\))
- set \(c1=0\).
Thus **yes, candidate 2 can match GT** (assuming \(\epsilon\ge 0\) so Abs drops).

3. Similar to 2 but includes an extra fixed \(+|\epsilon|^3\) (coefficient 1) that cannot be removed. You could absorb it into \(c2\) by setting \(c2\) accordingly because there is also \(c2|\epsilon|^3\). Indeed expression has \(c2|\epsilon|^3 + |\epsilon|^3 = (c2+1)|\epsilon|^3\), so it’s still adjustable. Also has \(|\epsilon|^4\) term removable by \(c1=0\). Exp term adjustable. So **also matchable**.

4. Like 2 but has extra \(c7\epsilon|\epsilon|^2 = c7\epsilon^3\) for \(\epsilon\ge 0\), which is just another adjustable \(\epsilon^3\) constant term; can set it to 0 or absorb. \(|\epsilon|^4\) removable. Exp term adjustable. **Matchable**.

5. Has \(T c0|\epsilon|^{c1}\) and also \(c4|\epsilon|^{c1}\): can set \(c1=3\) to create the needed \(T\epsilon^3\) and constant \(\epsilon^3\) pieces. Exp term adjustable to \(\epsilon^{0.47764}e^{-K/T}\). Must set the \(|\epsilon|^4\) and \(|\epsilon|^3\) extra terms \(c2,c3\) to 0. Then choose \(c0=7.64107\), \(c4=-7.64107\cdot 344.4596\). **Matchable**.

6. Has \(T c0\epsilon^3\) and exp term, but only \(|\epsilon|^4\) and \(|\epsilon|^3\) (not multiplied by \(T\)) are available: yes, it has \(c2|\epsilon|^3\) which can supply the constant \(\epsilon^3\) term; set \(c1=0\). Exp term adjustable. **Matchable**.

7. Same as 6 but with Abs on \(\epsilon^3\); under \(\epsilon\ge 0\) same. **Matchable**.

8. Uses \(T\epsilon^2\) and \(\epsilon^2\) terms, not \(\epsilon^3 T\). Cannot create \(T\epsilon^3\) for all \(\epsilon\). **No**.

9–134: Many have the right exp structure, but most have wrong \(T\epsilon^n\) power (often \(\epsilon^2\)), or include unavoidable extra functional forms (log, sin, cos, exp(T*c), exp(c*epsilon), rational in T/epsilon) that cannot be identically zero unless their coefficients are set to 0—yet even after zeroing, they often still lack either the \(T\epsilon^3\) term or the constant \(\epsilon^3\) term. However, since we already found matches, we only need existence of at least one match. Still, briefly:
- Any candidate with \(T*c0*\epsilon^3\) (or \(T*c0*|\epsilon|^3\)) **and** at least one free \(|\epsilon|^3\) (or equivalent) constant term **and** one exp term \(e^{c/T}|\epsilon|^{c}\) can be tuned to match (by setting all other coefficients to 0 and matching constants/exponents). This includes many early ones (2–7, 10, 14, 15, 17, 19, 20, 24, 25, 30, 35, 39, 41, 45, 48, 52–54, 60, 87, 89, 126, 129, etc.) *provided* they have an independent \(\epsilon^3\) (non-T) term available. Some do not.
- Candidates dominated by \(T*\epsilon^2\) families (65–86, 92, etc.) cannot match because GT’s polynomial part is in \(\epsilon^3\), not \(\epsilon^2\), and there’s no way to change the exponent by choosing constants.

Given candidate 2 (and several others) can be exactly tuned to GT under the plausible domain condition \(\epsilon\ge 0\), a match exists.

I need to compare each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `61.56*epsilon^0.4776*exp(-55.88/(8.314*T)) + epsilon^3 * 7.641*(T - 344.46)`

Expanding the GT:
`61.56*epsilon^0.4776*exp(-6.72/T) + 7.641*T*epsilon^3 - 2632.6*epsilon^3`

So GT = `c_A * epsilon^0.4776 * exp(-c_B/T) + c_C * T * epsilon^3 + c_D * epsilon^3`

where c_B = 55.88/8.314 ≈ 6.72.

The GT has three basis function terms:
1. `T * epsilon^3` (with coefficient ~7.641)
2. `epsilon^3` (with coefficient ~-2632.6)
3. `epsilon^0.4776 * exp(-c/T)` (Arrhenius-like term)

Now I need to check which candidates can match this structure. Under the domain constraint (epsilon ≥ 0), `|epsilon| = epsilon`.

Key requirements for a match:
- Must have `T * epsilon^3` term
- Must have `epsilon^3` term (constant coefficient)
- Must have `epsilon^c * exp(c/T)` term where the exponent c on epsilon is free (~0.4776)
- Must NOT have extra terms that can't be zeroed out (e.g., `epsilon^4` needs a free coefficient to set to 0)

Let me systematically check each candidate. For epsilon ≥ 0, |epsilon|^n = epsilon^n.

**Candidates with `T*c*epsilon^3` structure:**

**Candidate 1:** `T*c0*eps^3 + c1*eps^4 + c2*eps^3 + c3*eps/(c4*eps+c5) + c6/(c4*eps+c5) + c7*exp(c8/T)*eps^c9`
Has rational terms `c3*eps/(c4*eps+c5)` and `c6/(c4*eps+c5)` that can't generally be zeroed without making denominator infinite. Set c3=0, c6=0 to eliminate them. Then: `T*c0*eps^3 + c1*eps^4 + c2*eps^3 + c7*exp(c8/T)*eps^c9`. Set c1=0: matches GT structure.
Candidate 1 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 2:** `T*c0*eps^3 + c1*eps^4 + c2*eps^3 + c3*eps^3 + c4*exp(c5/T)*eps^c6`
Set c1=0, combine c2+c3 for eps^3 coefficient. This gives `T*c0*eps^3 + (c2+c3)*eps^3 + c4*exp(c5/T)*eps^c6`. Matches GT.
Candidate 2 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 3:** `T*c0*eps^3 + c1*eps^4 + c2*eps^3 + c3*exp(c4/T)*eps^c5 + eps^3`
Set c1=0. Then `T*c0*eps^3 + (c2+1)*eps^3 + c3*exp(c4/T)*eps^c5`. Matches GT.
Candidate 3 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 4:** `T*c0*eps^3 + c1*eps^4 + c2*eps^3 + c3*eps^3 + c4*exp(c5/T)*eps^c6 + c7*eps*eps^2`
c7*epsilon*|epsilon|^2 = c7*eps^3 for eps≥0. Set c1=0. Combine eps^3 terms: (c2+c3+c7). Matches GT.
Candidate 4 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 5:** `T*c0*eps^c1 + c2*eps^4 + c3*eps^3 + c4*eps^c1 + c5*exp(c6/T)*eps^c7`
Set c1=3, c2=0. Then `T*c0*eps^3 + c3*eps^3 + c4*eps^3 + c5*exp(c6/T)*eps^c7`. But wait - c1 is shared between T*c0*eps^c1 and c4*eps^c1. If c1=3, this works. Matches GT.
Candidate 5 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 6:** `T*c0*eps^3 + c1*eps^4 + c2*eps^3 + c3*exp(c4/T)*eps^c5`
Set c1=0. Matches GT.
Candidate 6 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 7:** `T*c0*eps^3 + c1*eps^4 + c2*eps^3 + c3*exp(c4/T)*eps^c5`
Same as Candidate 6 (with |epsilon| → epsilon for eps≥0). Set c1=0. Matches GT.
Candidate 7 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 8:** `T*eps^2 + c0*eps^4 + c1*eps^3 + c2*exp(c3/T)*eps^c4 + c5*eps^2`
The T*eps^2 term has coefficient 1 (fixed, not free). GT needs T*eps^3, not T*eps^2. Cannot match.
Candidate 8 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 9:** `T*c0*eps^3 + c1*eps^4 + c2*eps^3 + c3*exp(T*c4) + c5*eps^3 + c6*exp(c7/T)*eps^c8`
Set c1=0, c3=0 (or c4=0 making c3 a constant, but then it's a constant term not in GT). Actually set c3=0. Then matches GT.
Candidate 9 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 10:** `T*c0*eps^3 + c1*eps^4 + c2*eps^3 + c3*exp(T*c4) + c5*exp(c6/T)*eps^c7`
Set c1=0, c3=0. Matches GT.
Candidate 10 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 11:** `T*c0*eps^3 + c1*eps^4 + c2*eps + c3*eps^3 + c4*exp(c5/T)*eps^c6`
Set c1=0, c2=0. Matches GT.
Candidate 11 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 12:** `T*c0*eps^3 + c1*eps + c2*eps^4 + c3*eps^c4 + c5*exp(c6/T)*eps^c7`
Set c1=0, c2=0. Need eps^3 term: c3*eps^c4 with c4=3. Then `T*c0*eps^3 + c3*eps^3 + c5*exp(c6/T)*eps^c7`. Matches GT.
Candidate 12 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 13:** `T*c0*eps^3 + T*c1 + c2*eps^4 + c3 + c4*eps^3 + c5*eps^3 + c6*exp(c7/T)*eps^c8`
Set c1=0, c2=0, c3=0. Matches GT.
Candidate 13 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 14:** `T*c0*eps^3 + c1*eps^4 + c2*eps^3 + c3*exp(c4/T)*eps^c5 + c6*eps + c7`
Set c1=0, c6=0, c7=0. Matches GT.
Candidate 14 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 15:** `T*c0*eps^3 + T*c1 + c2*eps^4 + c3*eps^3 + c4*exp(c5/T)*eps^c6 + c7`

Candidate 23 verdict: [MATCH]

Candidate 25 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 26:** `T*c0*eps^3 + T*c1 + c2*eps^4 + c3 + c4*eps^3 + c5*eps^3 + c6*exp(c7/T)*eps^c8 + c9*eps`

Set c1=0, c7=0. Matches GT.
Candidate 27 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 28:** `T*c0*eps^3 + c1*eps^4 + c2*sin(c3*eps+c4) + c5*eps^3 + c6*eps^3 + c7*exp(c8/T)*eps^c9`

The last term c6*eps*(T+c7)^c8. Set c6=0, c1=0. Matches GT.
Candidate 30 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 31:** `T*c0*eps^3 + c1*eps^4 + c2*eps^3 + c3*log(c4*eps+1) + c5*exp(c6/T)*eps^c7`

Candidate 31 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 32:** `T*c0*eps^3 + c1*eps^4 + c2*eps^3 + c3*log(c4*eps+1) + c5*eps^3 + c6*exp(c7/T)*eps^c8`
Set c1=0, c3=0. Matches GT.
Candidate 32 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 33:** `T*c0*eps^3 + c1*eps^4 + c2/(eps+1)^2 + c3*eps^3 + c4*exp(c5/T)*eps^c6 + c7*eps + c7`
Note c7 appears twice (c7*eps + c7 = c7*(eps+1)). Set c1=0, c2=0, c7=0. Matches GT.
Candidate 33 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 34:** `T*c0*eps^3 + T*c1/(T*c2+c3) + c4*eps^4 + c5*eps^3 + c6*exp(c7/T)*eps^c8 + c9/(T*c2+c3)`
Set c1=0, c9=0, c4=0. Matches GT.
Candidate 34 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 35:** `T*c0*eps^3 + c1*eps^4 + c2*eps^3 + c3*exp(c4/T)*eps^c5 + c6*eps/(T*c7+c8) + c9/(T*c7+c8)`
Set c1=0, c6=0, c9=0. Matches GT.
Candidate 35 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 36:** `T*c0*eps^3 + c1*eps^4 + c2*eps^3 + c3*exp(c4/T)*eps^c5 + c6*sin(c7*log(c8*eps+1)+c9)`
